1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce answer.json** — Write ALL output to `/workspace/answer.json` with this structure:
   ```json
   {
     "analysis": {
       "summary": "Brief description of your approach",
       "files_examined": [{"path": "file.ext", "description": "..."}],
       "reasoning": "Detailed explanation or analysis"
     },
     "changes": [
       {"file": "path.ext", "description": "...", "diff": "unified diff"}
     ]
   }
   ```
   Omit `changes` if the task is analysis-only. Do NOT edit source files directly — produce diffs in `changes[]` instead.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Prometheus Metrics Exposition Pattern Across Kubernetes and Grafana

## Your Task

Find the Go source files in both kubernetes/kubernetes and grafana/grafana that implement the Prometheus metrics exposition pattern: where metrics are registered using the Prometheus client_golang library, how metric collectors are organized, and where the `/metrics` HTTP endpoint is configured to expose them. Compare how both projects structure their metrics infrastructure.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain. Both Kubernetes and Grafana use the Prometheus client_golang library to expose internal metrics, but they organize their metrics registration and exposition differently. Your goal is to map these patterns across both codebases.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/grafana--v11.4.0.


## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?
- **Symbol identification**: Correct symbol names and locations?
- **Keyword presence**: Did you mention key concepts (metrics registry, collectors, exposition)?

64-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Prometheus metrics exposition pattern across Kubernetes and Grafana. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've identified and analyzed **9 key files** and **24 important symbols** showing how both projects implement Prometheus metrics:

### **Kubernetes Approach:**
- **Centralized Registry**: Uses `legacyregistry` with a global `defaultRegistry` for metrics collection
- **Distributed Metric Definition**: Each module (audit, workqueue, etcd, etc.) registers its own metrics via `legacyregistry.MustRegister()`
- **Metrics Routes**: Metrics exposed through route installation classes (`DefaultMetrics`, `MetricsWithReset`)
- **Metrics Provider Pattern**: Pluggable providers for components like workqueue and leader election

### **Grafana Approach:**
- **Centralized Metric Definition**: All metrics declared in `pkg/infra/metrics/metrics.go`
- **Service-Based Management**: Uses Wire dependency injection for metrics initialization and gathering
- **Separate HTTP Server**: Runs metrics on an independent instrumentation server (separate port)
- **Multi-Registry Pattern**: Combines Kubernetes legacyregistry with Prometheus default gatherer via custom `multiRegistry` and `addPrefixWrapper`

### **Key Differences:**
1. **HTTP Integration**: Kubernetes integrates metrics into main API server; Grafana uses separate server
2. **Metric Namespace**: Kubernetes uses subsystems; Grafana wraps with "grafana_" prefix
3. **Dependency Injection**: Grafana uses Wire; Kubernetes uses global init() patterns
4. **Configuration**: Kubernetes distributed by module; Grafana centralized in one file

The analysis has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file listings, symbol references, and detailed narrative explanation.

Exposition Pattern: Kubernetes vs Grafana\\n\\n### Overview\\n\\nBoth Kubernetes and Grafana implement the Prometheus metrics exposition pattern using the prometheus/client_golang library, but they organize their metrics infrastructure differently based on their architectural needs.\\n\\n### Kubernetes Architecture\\n\\n**Registry Management (legacyregistry):**\\nKubernetes uses a centralized metrics registry pattern in `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go`. The key components are:\\n\\n- **defaultRegistry**: A single global `metrics.NewKubeRegistry()` that serves as the central metrics repository\\n- **DefaultGatherer**: Exposes the gatherer interface for collecting metrics\\n- **Handler() and HandlerWithReset()**: Factory functions that return HTTP handlers instrumented with `promhttp.InstrumentMetricHandler()`\\n- **MustRegister**: Global function that registers metrics with the default registry\\n\\nThe registry automatically includes Go runtime and process metrics via collectors registered in the init() function (line 54-56), and includes Kubernetes-specific prometheus extensions.\\n\\n**Metrics Routes (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/routes/metrics.go):**\\nKubernetes exposes metrics via route installation classes:\\n\\n- **DefaultMetrics**: Installs `/metrics` endpoint using `legacyregistry.Handler()`\\n- **MetricsWithReset**: Installs `/metrics` endpoint with DELETE method support via `legacyregistry.HandlerWithReset()`\\n- **register() function**: Explicitly registers multiple metric collectors:\\n  - apimetrics.Register()\\n  - cachermetrics.Register()\\n  - etcd3metrics.Register()\\n  - flowcontrolmetrics.Register()\\n  - peerproxymetrics.Register()\\n  - handlersmetrics.Register()\\n\\n**Distributed Metric Definition Pattern:**\\nKubernetes defines metrics across many modules using a consistent pattern. Example from `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/metrics.go`:\\n\\n- Metrics are defined as package-level variables (eventCounter, errorCounter, levelCounter, ApiserverAuditDroppedCounter)\\n- Each metric uses `metrics.NewCounter()` or `metrics.NewCounterVec()` with metadata (Subsystem, Name, Help, StabilityLevel)\\n- Metrics are registered in init() functions via `legacyregistry.MustRegister()`\\n- StabilityLevel is enforced for metric governance\\n\\n**Metrics Provider Pattern:**\\nKubernetes uses interface-based metric providers for pluggable metrics. In `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/prometheus/workqueue/metrics.go`, the `prometheusMetricsProvider` struct implements provider interfaces that allow components like workqueue and leader election to emit metrics without direct dependencies on prometheus.\\n\\n### Grafana Architecture\\n\\n**Metric Definition (pkg/infra/metrics/metrics.go):**\\nGrafana declares all metrics as package-level variables in a single metrics definition file:\\n\\n- **ExporterName constant**: Set to \\\"grafana\\\" as the namespace for metrics\\n- **Metric Variables**: Declared directly (e.g.,
